25:T5e90,<entryFree id="n14878" key="رَجَعَ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">رَجَعَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">رَجِعَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رُجُوعٌ</foreign> (S, Msb, K, &amp;c.) and <foreign lang="ar">رَجْعٌ</foreign>, (M, Msb,) but the former is that which commonly obtains and is agreeable with analogy as inf. n. of the intrans. v., and the latter as inf. n. of the trans. v., (MF, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَرْجَعٌ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K, &amp;c.,) which is anomalous, because inf. ns. [of this kind] of verbs of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعَلَ</foreign> having the <pb n="1038"/> aor. of the measure <foreign lang="ar">يَفْعِلُ</foreign> are [by rule] only with fet-h [to the medial radical], (S, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَرْجِعَةٌ</foreign>, which is in like manner anomalous, (K,) and <foreign lang="ar">رُجْعَى</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) [not <foreign lang="ar">رُجْعًى</foreign> as in the Lexicons of Golius and Freytag,] and <foreign lang="ar">رُجْعَانٌ</foreign>, (K,) <hi rend="ital">He returned; he went,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">came, back</hi> [to the same place, or person, or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  state, or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  occupation, or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  action, or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  saying, &amp;c.]; <hi rend="ital">he reverted; contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ذَهَبَ</foreign>; (ISk, Msb;) <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">انْصَرَفَ</foreign>: (K:) <foreign lang="ar">رُجُوعٌ</foreign> signifies the <hi rend="ital">returning to a former place,</hi> or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">quality,</hi> or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">state;</hi> (Kull p. 196;) the <hi rend="ital">returning to that from which was the commencement,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">from which the commencement is supposed to have been, whether it be a place,</hi> or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">an action,</hi> or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">a saying, and whether the returning be by the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">whole</hi>] <hi rend="ital">person or thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by a part thereof,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by an action thereof.</hi> (Er-Rághib.) Hence the saying in the Kur [lxiii. 8], <foreign lang="ar">لَئِنْ رَجَعْنَا إِلَى المَدِينَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Verily if we return to the city</hi>]. (Er-Rághib.) And [in the same, xii. 63,] <foreign lang="ar">فَلَمَّا رَجَعُوا إِلَى أَبِيهِمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And when they returned to their father</hi>]. (Idem.) And in the same, [vi. 164, and xxxix. 9,] <foreign lang="ar">ثُمَّ إِلَى رَبِّكُمْ مَرْجِعُكُمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Then unto your Lord shall be your return</hi>]: (S:) the like of which occurs in the same, vi. 60: but it may be either from [the intrans. inf. n.] <foreign lang="ar">رُجُوعٌ</foreign> or from [the trans.] <foreign lang="ar">رَجْعٌ</foreign>: (Er-Rághib:) it cannot be a n. of place, because it is made trans. by means of <foreign lang="ar">إِلَى</foreign>, and also because it occurs in the Kur [v. 53, &amp;c.], followed by <foreign lang="ar">جَمِيعًا</foreign>, as a denotative of state: (L:) in like manner <foreign lang="ar">الرُّجْعَى</foreign> also occurs in the Kur xcvi. 8. (TA.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَتِ المَرْأَةُ إِلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَهْلِهَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The woman returned to her family</hi> by reason of the death of her husband or by reason of divorcement. (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ إِلَى الصِّحَّةِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He returned to soundness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">health</hi>], or <foreign lang="ar">المَرَضِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">disease,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sickness</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">إِلَى حَالَةِ الفَقْرِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">to the state of poverty</hi>], or <foreign lang="ar">الغِنَى</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">wealth,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">competence,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sufficiency</hi>]. (Kull p. 196.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَوْدَهُ عَلَى بَدْئِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He returned in the way by which he had come.</hi> (Kull ibid.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ مِنْ سَفَرِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He returned from his journey.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ عَنِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأِمْرِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He returned</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">reverted</hi>] <hi rend="ital">from the affair.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ عَنِ الشَّىْءِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He left,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">relinquished, the thing.</hi> (Kull p. 197.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ عَنِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الذَّنْبِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He relinquished sin;</hi> i. e.] <hi rend="ital">he repented;</hi> and so <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ</foreign> alone, agreeably with the usage in the Kur iii. 65, &amp;c. (Er-Rághib.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  [Several other phrases, in which this verb occurs, will be found in other arts.: as <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ عَلَى ظَهْرِهِ</foreign> in art. <foreign lang="ar">ظهر</foreign>: <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعْتُ القَهْقَرَى</foreign> in art. <foreign lang="ar">قهقر</foreign>: <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ دَرَجَهُ</foreign>, and variations thereof, in art. <foreign lang="ar">درج</foreign>: &amp;c.]          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ إِلَيْهِ</foreign> [sometimes signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ عَلَيْهِ</foreign>] <hi rend="ital">He returned against him; he returned to attack him.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">صَرَمّنِى ثُمَّ رَجَعَ يَكَلِّمُنِى</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He cut me,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ceased to speak to me; then he returned to speaking to me</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">خَالَفَنِى ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إِلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَوْلِى</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He opposed me,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">disagreed with me; then he returned,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">had regard, to my saying</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">مَا رُجِعَ إِلَيْهِ فِى خَطْبٍ إِلَّا كَفَى</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Re course was not had to him in an affair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an affliction, but he sufficed.</hi>] (TA.) [<foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ إِلَيْهِ</foreign> often means <hi rend="ital">He had recourse,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he recurred, to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="13">-b13-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ بِهِ عَلَى شَرِيكِهِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He made a claim for restitution of it upon his co-partner.</hi> (IAth, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">خلط</foreign>.) (Mgh.) [All these significations are well known, as pertaining to the two verbs here mentioned, and of frequent occurrence in classical and postclassical writings: and hence several phrases here following.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  See 1, last quarter of the paragraph, in five places.          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Hence, (Mgh,) <foreign lang="ar">التَّرْجِيعُ</foreign>

                  <foreign lang="ar">اذان</foreign>

                  <foreign lang="ar">اذان</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">once to repeat them.</hi> (Msb: [but this is a strange explanation; and probably corrupted by a copyist: it seems that, instead of “ to repeat them, ” we should read “ <hi rend="ital">and repeated them.</hi> ”])          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [Hence also,] <foreign lang="ar">التَّرْجِيعُ</foreign>, (K, TA,) or <foreign lang="ar">تَرْجِيعُ الصَّوْتِ</foreign>, (S,) <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">The act of quavering,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">trilling; rapidly repeating many times one very short note,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">each note of a piece;</hi> a general characteristic of Arabian chanting and singing and piping, and often continued throughout the whole performance;] <hi rend="ital">the reiterating</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">تَرْدِيد</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">of the voice in the throat,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fauces,</hi> (S, K, TA,) <hi rend="ital">like</hi> [<hi rend="ital">as is done in</hi>] <hi rend="ital">chanting,</hi> (S,) or <hi rend="ital">which is practised in reading</hi> or <hi rend="ital">reciting,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">singing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">piping,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">other performances, of such as are accompanied with quavering,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">trilling:</hi> (TA:) or, as some say, <hi rend="ital">the mutual approximation of the various kinds of movements in the voice:</hi> 'Abd-Allah Ibn-Mughaffal, in his <foreign lang="ar">ترجيع</foreign>, by the prolonging of the voice, in reading, or reciting, imitated the like of <foreign lang="ar">آا آا آا</foreign>.
